<binary blob: %u bytes>
<br><b>NOTE</b>: As this is an animation modifier, it can be applied at the folder level to all animation nodes contained in it.
<br><b>NOTE</b>: Can only discard an entire bone channel, not just the translation, rotation or scale components.
<br>If Static Only is checked the animation channel must also be static, i.e. Channel's value doesn't change during the animation.
<br>Name can be a wildcard glob, i.e. use * to discard all channels of the specified type.
<br>The channel will end up with the bind pose value as defined by the model.
<empty member name>
<fmod
<font color="red">Face is connected to itself, cannot dissolve</font>
<font color='darkred'><strong>Off:</strong></font> Maintain the relative translation and rotation between the source file origin and the parent bone's bind pose.<br><font color='darkgreen'><strong>On:</strong></font> Realign the translation and rotation of the source file to match the parent bone exactly.<br><br><em>(NOTE: The 'Offset Origin' and 'Offset Angle' are applied in either case.)</em>
<font color='red'>(WARNING: Performance risk!)</font><br>Indicates this breakpiece is essential for gameplay or other reasons.<br>Forces the piece to always spawn, potentially suppressing other breakpieces to stay in-budget.

<li>3 implicit animations
<li>@<strong>&lt;NAME&gt;</strong>_lookFrame_0 :: ( Frame 0 ) - ( Frame 1 )</li>
<li>@<strong>&lt;NAME&gt;</strong>_lookFrame_1 :: ( Frame 1 ) - ( Frame 1 ) - Note that this is an empty animation</li>
<li>@<strong>&lt;NAME&gt;</strong>_lookFrame_2 :: ( Frame 2 ) - ( Frame 1 )</li>
<li>A 1D Blend additive sequence with pose parameter values [-1, 0, 1]
<li>A pose parameter named "turn" by default with the range [-1, 1]</li>
<li>Frame 0 :: Left Pose</li>
<li>Frame 1 :: Center Pose</li>
<li>Frame 2 :: Right Pose</li>
<li>The 1D Blend sequence should be applied to runs with an AddLayer <img src='game:tools/images/modeldoc_editor/outliner_icon_addlayer.png' /> node</li>
<li>[ @_lookFrame_0, @_lookFrame_1, @_lookFrame_2 ]</li>
<map_key>
<map_value>
<no failure reason set>
<p>Loads a content file containing animation keyframe data and resolves into animation data which plays in reverse, i.e. backwards.</p><p>Works the same as AnimFile except the direction of the animation data.</p><p>When specifying a sub frame range, the frame range is pulled from the animation file before reversal.</p><p>For a typical walk style animation with extracted motion, likely an AnimAlign to first frame of the original forward animation will be required.</p>

Applies a bone scale set to the animation over the specified frame range specified by the 2D animation curve.<br>The Input Range is the X Axis range (horizontal) and corresponds to the frame range.<br>The Output Range is the Y Axis range (vertical) and is the scale set weight value over the frame range.<br>Any frames which fall outside of the frame range are left alone.<br><center><br><img src='game:tools/images/modeldoc_editor/docs_anim_markup_curve.png'/><br></center>AnimForceBoneScaleSet nodes are processed in the order they appear under the AnimFile node and will overwrite previously written data if the frame ranges overlap.<b>NOTE</b>: Although the Input/Frame Range are floats, integers should be used. Curve data is not evaluated at run time. The curve is sampled once per frame of the animation and the values are linearly interpolated between frames.<br>
Applies an animation markup over a specified frame range with a value controlled by an editable 2D animation curve.<br>The Input Range is the X Axis range (horizontal) and corresponds to the frame range.<br>The Output Range is the Y Axis range (vertical) and is the value over the frame range.<br>Any frames which fall outside of the frame range are left alone.<br><center>
Applies to morph animation only.<br><br>This is the per component precision threshold to try and attain when optimizing the bit rate. If the error is below the precision threshold, we will remove bits until we reach it without exceeding it. If the error is above the precision threshold, we will add more bits until we lower it underneath. 
Applies to skeletal animation only.<br><br>See :: https://github.com/nfrechette/acl/blob/develop/docs/compressing_a_raw_clip.md<br><br>The last important setting to choose is the error_threshold. This is used in conjunction with the error metric and the virtual vertex distance from the skeleton in order to guarantee that a certain quality is maintained. A default value of 0.01cm (or ~0.004 inches in game units) is safe to use and it most likely should never be changed unless the units you are using differ. If you do run into issues where compression artifacts are visible, in all likelihood the virtual vertex distance used on the problematic bones is not conservative enough.
Applies to skeletal animation only.<br><br>Specify how aggressively to attempt to reduce the memory footprint. Higher levels will try more permutations and bit rates. The higher the level, the slower the compression but the smaller the memory footprint. <br><b>NOTE</b>: Currently lowest, low and medium are all equivalent.
Applies to skeletal animation only.<br><br>https://github.com/nfrechette/acl/blob/develop/docs/creating_a_skeleton.md<br><br>The virtual vertex distance is used by the error metric function. It will measure the error of a vertex at that particular distance from the bone in object space. This distance should be large enough to contain the vast majority of the visible vertices skinned on that particular bone. The algorithm ensures that all vertices contained up to this distance will have an error lower than the supplied error threshold in the CompressionSettings. It is generally sufficient for this value to be approximate and it is often safe to use the same value for every bone in humanoid characters. A value of 3cm (or ~1 inch in game units) is good enough for cinematographic quality for most characters. While visible vertices around the torso will often be further away than this, finger tips and facial bones will be closer than that. Because the compressed track data is stored in relative space of the parent bone, any error will accumulate down the hierarchy. This means that in order to keep the leaf bones within that accuracy threshold, all the parent bones in that chain will require even higher accuracy.
